Notes from the slides:

  "based at address 0x0001_0000 in volatile memory" - check this...
  "size requirements: code can reside between 0x1_0000 and 0x1_c000"...
  "$sp = 0x1_c000"
    but we are at 0x0800_0000?

  InVitroDbg - uses a modified qemu, interacts with NIC.
  InVivoDbg  - real debugger, controls firmware executed on NIC.
    halt
    resume
    hbp

    Step-by-step, memory access tracing:
    "Does not rely on firmware code analysis; extracts the very core behaviour
     of the firmware"

  "CPU registers found in non-documented NIC registers"

  "EEPROM format contains [...] voltages" <- ???

  CPU reset vector is 0x4000_0000. "execute-only" memory area
  "A non-documented device register holds the current dword pointed by pc;
   dump the ROM by modifying $pc and polling this register"

  Some things are just wrong:
    States that MAC configuration is done in stage2, actually it is done
    in stage1...

  "The EEPROM header is CRC32-checked by ROM code
   The ROM code for BCM5721 is bugged
   Performs CRC over whole header including CRC field
   Compares with static constant inlined in the assembly code
   Bruteforce the CRC32 field until it matches the constant..."

PCIe View:

                                                RX CPU Addr
                                                -----------
  BAR1/2   +0x0000_0000: Registers              0xC000_xxxx
           +0x0000_8000: Memory Window (32k)    N/A
               Window base controlled by
               Memory Window Base Address register
  -------- +0x0001_0000: Window and BAR End ----------------------
  BAR3/4   APE Registers/Memory/etc.   (64k)    0xC001_xxxx

  -----------------------------------------------------------------
  BAR5/6   ??? Seems to have something (64k)
           to do with MSI-X.
  -----------------------------------------------------------------
  OptROM                              (256k)

  -----------------------------------------------------------------

Access all memory:
  TG3PCI_MEM_WIN_BASE_ADDR
    This controls both the memory window base and the indirect access
    address used by TG3PCI_MEM_WIN_DATA.

  TG3PCI_MEM_WIN_DATA         - contains/sets 32-bit word pointed to by BASE_ADDR
  tg3 driver uses this to access GENCOM


  "Flat view": See p. 184. There's a bit in REG_PCI_STATE which can change the
  BAR from mapping a 64 KiB range to a 32 MiB. But Linux doesn't use this, so
  let's ignore it, it will make trying to debug from userspace difficult.

  Below: W+x = From start of address space accessed by window and window base register.
    e.g. to access W+0, set window base to 0 and access BAR1+32k+0 (start of window).

---- APE/Driver Communication Procedures -------------------------------------------------
Driver 'scratchpad' read:
  NOTE: This 'scratchpad' appears completely unrelated to the 0xC003_0000
  scratchpad above. It uses an area in APE SHM and the APE event messaging
  system.

  NCSI support; APE FW magic correct ('APE!'); REG_APE__FW_STATUS__READY is asserted;
  bufoff = APE_SHM_BASE + GetReg(REG_APE__SEG_MSG_BUF_OFF);
  msgoff = bufoff + 2*sizeof(uint32_t);
  maxlen = GetReg(REG_APE__SEG_MSG_BUF_LEN);
  Wait for any pending event to complete first.
  SetReg(REG_APE__EVENT_STATUS, DRIVER_EVENT|SCRATCHPAD_READ|EVENT_PENDING);
  SetReg(APE_REG(bufoff),   baseoff);
  SetReg(APE_REG(bufoff+4), length);
  mem unlock
  SetReg(REG_APE__EVENT, APE_EVENT_1);
  Wait for pending event to complete.
  Read length words beginning at msgoff.

The driver-accessed 'scratchpad' seems to have the following layout and appears
to relate to hardware monitoring (temperature, etc.):
  0x0000:   tg3_ocir structure no. 0 (magic: 0x5253434F, 'OCSR') (64 bytes)
    See tg3_ocir.
  0x0040:   tg3_ocir structure no. 1
  0x0080:   tg3_ocir structure no. 2
  0x00C0:   End of OCIR structures
  0x00C8:   Caution Temperature (u32)
  0x00CC:   Maximum Temperature (u32)
  0x00D4:   Temperature Reading (u32)

To send APE event:
  Wait for pending event to complete.
  SetReg(REG_APE__EVENT_STATUS, REG_APE__EVENT_STATUS__PENDING|...);
  Unlock APE (LOCK_MEM).
  SetReg(REG_APE__EVENT, REG_APE_EVENT__1);

To send driver event:
  Initialize REG_APE__HOST_* if not initialized ('HOST' magic, etc.)
  Write REG_APE__HOST_DRIVER_STATE.
  Send APE event (REG_APE__EVENT_STATUS__DRIVER_EVENT|REG_APE__EVENT_STATUS__STATE_CHANGE).

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Note: Linux TG3 driver has some firmware images, but they are for older
Broadcom NICs to enable TSO. BCM5719 doesn't need them

GENCOM (1KiB) (base=$k0=0xB50)

1 0xB50  0x000  sometimes BOOTCODE_READY_MAGIC (tg3: "NIC_SRAM_FIRMWARE_MBOX")
                  "Write the T3_MAGIC_NUMBER to the device memory at offset
                   0xB50 to notify the bootcode that the reset is a warm
                   reset (driver initiated core_clocks reset)."
                  "poll the general communication memory at 0xB50 for the
                   ones complement of the T3_MAGIC_NUMBER."
1 0xB54  0x004  sometimes BOOTCODE_READY_MAGIC (tg3: "NIC_SRAM_DATA_SIG")
1 0xB58  0x008  TG3 NIC_SRAM_DATA_CFG. Flags:
                  0000 0000  00ag 000x  0f0m 000E  AWPP LL00
                  W: WOL Enable
                  A: ASF Enable
                  E: EEPROM write-protect           (TG3: EEPROM_WP)
                  m: Mini-PCI
                  f: Fiber WOL
                  x: PXE Boot Agent Related
                  g: No GPIO2
                  a: APE Enable
                  LL: LED Mode
                    0x0000_0000: LED Mode: MAC
                    0x0000_0004: LED Mode: PHY1
                    0x0000_0008: LED Mode: PHY2
                  PP: PHY Type
                    0x0000_0000: PHY Type: Unknown  (TG3: PHY_TYPE_UNKNOWN)
                    0x0000_0010: PHY Type: GPHY     (TG3: PHY_TYPE_COPPER)
                    0x0000_0020: PHY Type: SERDES   (TG3: PHY_TYPE_FIBER)
                    0x20 if SERDES, based on 0x1E4's LSB otherwise
1 0xB5C  0x00C  TG3: NIC_SRAM_DATA_VER. unusual 16-bit field
1        0x00E  ---
1        0x020  partly set from 0x1E4
1 0xB74  0x024  TG3: NIC_SRAM_DATA_PHY_ID. Can be 0x5A5A5A5A, or MII PHY_IDENTIFIER value.
  0xB78  0x028  TG3: NIC_SRAM_FW_CMD_MBOX.
                  TG3 values:
                    FWCMD_NICDRV_ALIVE         0x0000_0001
                    FWCMD_NICDRV_PAUSE_FW      0x0000_0002
                    FWCMD_NICDRV_IPV4ADDR_CHG  0x0000_0003
                    FWCMD_NICDRV_IPV6ADDR_CHG  0x0000_0004
                    FWCMD_NICDRV_FIX_DMAR      0x0000_0005
                    FWCMD_NICDRV_FIX_DMAW      0x0000_0006
                    FWCMD_NICDRV_LINK_UPDATE   0x0000_000C
                    FWCMD_NICDRV_ALIVE2        0x0000_000D
                    FWCMD_NICDRV_ALIVE3        0x0000_000E
  0xB7C  0x02C  NIC_SRAM_FW_CMD_LEN_MBOX
  0xB80  0x030  NIC_SRAM_FW_CMD_DATA_MBOX

 20xC00  0x0B0  NIC_SRAM_FW_ASF_STATUS_MBOX. sometimes BOOTCODE_READY_MAGIC
1 0xC04  0x0B4  NIC_SRAM_FW_DRV_STATE_MBOX. ... can be 0
                  Device Closing Procedure: "write 0x2 to the device memory;
                  write 0x80000002 to the device memory."
                  TG3:
                    DRV_STATE_START:        0x0000_0001
                    DRV_STATE_START_DONE:   0x8000_0001
                    DRV_STATE_UNLOAD:       0x0000_0002
                    DRV_STATE_UNLOAD_DONE:  0x8000_0002
                    DRV_STATE_WOL:          0x0000_0003
                    DRV_STATE_SUSPEND:      0x0000_0004
1 0xC08  0x0B8  TG3: NIC_SRAM_FW_RESET_TYPE_MBOX. some values: 1, 2
1        0x0BC  upper16 are a field... one value: 0xFEFE0008
                stage2 sets at start: 0xFEFE0009

1 0xC18  0x0C8  TG3: NIC_SRAM_MAC_ADDR_LOW_MBOX. MAC0 low bits

                related to fastboot. some fields:

         0x350  OTG ONLY: Debug Boot Protocol. Indicates GEN [0x354-0x35C] are valid if set to 0xDECAFBAD.
         0x354  OTG ONLY: Debug Boot Protocol. s1ImageSize. Valid only if GEN 0x350 is set to the magic.
         0x358  OTG ONLY: Debug Boot Protocol. s1ImageOffset. Valid only if GEN 0x350 is set to the magic.
         0x35C  OTG ONLY: Debug Boot Protocol. s2ImageSize. Valid only if GEN 0x350 is set to the magic.
         0x360  OTG ONLY: Debug Output Protocol. Up to four ASCII bytes are written into this 32-bit word.
         0x364  OTG ONLY: Debug Output Protocol. Set to 1 once GEN 0x360 word has been written. The bootcode
                          waits until it is written back to 0 by the host to acknowledge receipt of the ASCII
                          bytes before writing more output. Debug output is only generated if
                          GEN 0x368 is set to 0xDECAFBAD.
         0x368  OTG ONLY: Debug Output Protocol. Host attachment indicator. Set to 0xDECAFBAD to indicate
                          that debug output should be generated, otherwise bootcode will not wait for log
                          output to be received/acknowledged by host.

 2      0x2DE8  boolean flag involved in S2MainLoop2
 2      0x2DEC  0x2DE8 moved here in v1.45
 2      0x2DF0  APE-related

       __ write access to the following seems to be guarded by APE_CONTROL_REGISTER_WRITE_ENABLE _______
       0x4100  I'm naming this: TG3_APE_RCPU_SEG_SIG. confirmed: expect APE_RCPU_MAGIC
               'i' on fields below indicate they are zeroed if APE_RCPU_MAGIC is not present
               Other fields tend to get initialized always.
       0x4104  I'm naming this: TG3_APE_RCPU_SEG_LEN, confirmed value: 0x34
     i 0x4108  I'm naming this: TG3_APE_RCPU_INIT_COUNT (see 0x4208 and 'RCPU' magic above vs. 'HOST' magic below)
               incremented on each init, boot counter? ] 0x4100==APE_RCPU_MAGIC indicates these are initialized...
                                                       ] cleared to 0 on initialization
       0x410C  RX CPU firmware version (0x0127 -> v1.39).
       0x4110  Set to GEN_CFG_FEATURE (GEN 1E4).
       0x4114  Set to REG 0x6434 (PCI Vendor/Device ID) (lower/upper 16 bits are swapped)
       0x4118  Set to REG 0x6438 (PCI Subsystem ID) (not swapped)
     i 0x411C  The frobnicating routine increments this.
     i 0x4120  The frobnicating routine writes to this.
     i 0x4124  The frobnicating routine copies APE 0x400C to this.
       0x4128  Set to GEN_CFG_HW   (GEN 1E8).
       0x412C  Set to GEN_CFG_HW_2 (GEN 2A8).
       0x4130  Set to g_cpmuStatus (if g_cpmuStatus is initialized, indicated by lower16==0x362C==REG_STATUS)
               g_cpmuStatus comes from GEN_CPMU_STATUS, which comes from REG_STATUS (upper16)/0x362C (lower16)
       _________________________________________________________________________________________________
       0x4200  TG3_APE_HOST_SEG_SIG (magic: "HOST")
       0x4204  TG3_APE_HOST_SEG_LEN (magic: 0x0000_0020)
       0x4208  TG3_APE_HOST_INIT_COUNT
       0x420C  TG3_APE_HOST_DRIVER_ID (Linux: 0xF0MM_mm00, M: major version, m: minor version)
       0x4210  TG3_APE_HOST_BEHAVIOR
                 0x0000_0001:  APE_HOST_BEHAV_NO_PHYLOCK
       0x4214  TG3_APE_HOST_HEARTBEAT_INT_MS
                    0:  APE_HOST_HEARTBEAT_INT_DISABLE
                 5000:  APE_HOST_HEARTBEAT_INT_5SEC
       0x4218  TG3_APE_HOST_HEARTBEAT_COUNT
       0x421C  TG3_APE_HOST_DRVR_STATE
                 0x0000_0001: TG3_APE_HOST_DRVR_STATE_START
                 0x0000_0002: TG3_APE_HOST_DRVR_STATE_UNLOAD
                 0x0000_0003: TG3_APE_HOST_DRVR_STATE_WOL
       0x4224  TG3_APE_HOST_WOL_SPEED
                 0x0000_8000: TG3_APE_HOST_WOL_SPEED_AUTO
       0x4300  TG3_APE_EVENT_STATUS
                 0x0000_0010: APE_EVENT_STATUS_DRIVER_EVNT
                 0x0000_0500: APE_EVENT_STATUS_STATE_CHNGE
                 0x0000_1600: APE_EVENT_STATUS_SCRTCHPD_READ
                 0x0000_1700: APE_EVENT_STATUS_SCRTCHPD_WRITE
                 0x0001_0000: APE_EVENT_STATUS_STATE_START
                 0x0002_0000: APE_EVENT_STATUS_STATE_UNLOAD
                 0x0003_0000: APE_EVENT_STATUS_STATE_WOL
                 0x0004_0000: APE_EVENT_STATUS_STATE_SUSPEND
                 0x8000_0000: APE_EVENT_STATUS_EVENT_PENDING
   s1  0x4308  Can be APE_PROT_MAGIC ("PROT"), in which case the following two fields are valid.
               My name: REG_APE__PROT_MAGIC
   s1  0x4314  Stage1 gets high bits of MAC0 from here. ???
               My name: REG_APE__PROT_MAC0_HIGH
   s1  0x4318  Stage1 gets  low bits of MAC0 from here. ???
               My name: REG_APE__PROT_MAC0_LOW

       0x8400  TG3_APE_PER_LOCK_REQ
                 0x0000_1000: APELOCK_PER_REQ_DRIVER
       0x8420  TG3_APE_PER_LOCK_GRANT
                 0x0000_1000: APE_PER_LOCK_GRANT_DRIVER

// All fields are big endian unless otherwise specified.

tag type 0x00: PCI Expansion ROM pointer, pointer in body word v1
  (BMAPI_FW_CODE_IMAGE_TYPE_PXE)

0x01  BMAPI_FW_CODE_IMAGE_TYPE_ASF_INIT
0x02  BMAPI_FW_CODE_IMAGE_TYPE_ASF_CPUA
0x03  BMAPI_FW_CODE_IMAGE_TYPE_ASF_CPUB
0x04  BMAPI_FW_CODE_IMAGE_TYPE_ASF_CFG
0x05  BMAPI_FW_CODE_IMAGE_TYPE_ISCSI_CFG
  iSCSI configuration for function 0.
0x06  BMAPI_FW_CODE_IMAGE_TYPE_ISCSI_CFG_PRG
  iSCSI configuration program.
0x07  BMAPI_FW_CODE_IMAGE_TYPE_USER_BLOCK
0x08  BMAPI_FW_CODE_IMAGE_TYPE_BRSF_BLOCK
0x09  BMAPI_FW_CODE_IMAGE_TYPE_ISCSI_BOOT
  iSCSI boot program.
0x0A  BMAPI_FW_CODE_IMAGE_TYPE_ASF_MBOX
0x0B  BMAPI_FW_CODE_IMAGE_TYPE_ISCSI_CFG_1
  iSCSI configuration for function 1.
0x0C  BMAPI_FW_CODE_IMAGE_TYPE_APE_CFG
0x0D  BMAPI_FW_CODE_IMAGE_TYPE_APE_CODE
  The APE code. e.g. NCSI APE image.
0x0E  BMAPI_FW_CODE_IMAGE_TYPE_APE_UPDATE
0x0F  BMAPI_FW_CODE_IMAGE_TYPE_EXT_CFG
0x10  BMAPI_FW_CODE_IMAGE_TYPE_EXT_DIR
  Used to provide more directory entries. Tag types with the MSG set (0x80-0xFF)
  MUST be located in an extended directory and not in a normal directory; likewise,
  tag types without the MSB set should not be located in an extended directory.

0x11  BMAPI_FW_CODE_IMAGE_TYPE_APE_DATA /* aka Opaque Management Data, Offline Mailbox Data */
0x12  BMAPI_FW_CODE_IMAGE_TYPE_APE_WEB_DATA /* Web/HTML interface content */
0x13  BMAPI_FW_CODE_IMAGE_TYPE_APE_WORKAROUND /* APE workaround firmware */

0x14  BMAPI_FW_CODE_IMAGE_TYPE_EXTENDED_VPD
  Used to designate the location of the optional extended VPD block
  on the flash.

  Extended Directory Types:
0x88
  Appears to be CCM code (Comprehensive Configuration Management, program which can
  be loaded and run by the PXE option ROM if the user presses a key during boot).
0x82
  iSCSI configuration for function 2.
0x83
  iSCSI configuration for function 3.



typedef struct {
  uint32_t header; // high 8 bits: identifier, low 8 bits: tag valid if nonzero...
  uint32_t v1, v2;
} tag; // 12 bytes

struct {
/*  00*/ uint32_t magic;           // 0x669955AA
/*  04*/ uint32_t s1Entrypoint;    // Stage 1 entrypoint address in RAM.
/*  08*/ uint32_t s1Size;          // Stage 1 size IN WORDS. Slightly off?
/*  0C*/ uint32_t s1Offset;        // Offset to start of stage 1 code in file.
                                   // This is the on-flash start of the stage1 code,
                                   // which must be loaded to address s1Entrypoint.
/*  10*/ uint32_t UNKNOWN;         // 0x252333D4
/*  14*/ uint32_t UNKNOWN;         // 0x00000007
/*  18*/ tag      tags[8];
                  // tags[0]: 0x0D.002F5B 00004C14 00000000
                  //   0x0D: NCSI APE Image Pointer
                  //     0x  00_2F5B: NCSI Image Length (in words)
                  //     0x0000_4C14: Offset to NCSI image in flash
                  //     0x0000_0000: Probably unused
                  // tags[1..7]: all zeroes
/*  78*/ // end of tag space (exclusive)
/*  78*/ uint32_t UNKNOWN;         // 0
/*  7C*/ uint32_t mac0[2];         // MAC. mac0[0] upper 16 bits are zero/unused.
/*  84*/ char     name[16];        // "BCM95719", zero padded
/*  94*/ uint32_t UNKNOWN;         // 41 30 01 2b
/*  98*/ uint32_t UNKNOWN;         // 0
/*  9C*/ uint32_t UNKNOWN;         // 0
/*  A0*/ uint16_t pciDevice0;      // 0x1657
/*  A2*/ uint16_t pciVendor0;      // 0x14e4
/*  A4*/ uint16_t pciDevice1;      // 0x1657
/*  A6*/ uint16_t pciVendor1;      // 0x14e4
/*  A8*/ uint32_t UNKNOWN;         // 00 42 00 00
/*  AC*/ uint32_t UNKNOWN;         // 0

/*  B0*/ uint32_t UNKNOWN;         // 0
         uint32_t UNKNOWN;         // 0
         uint32_t UNKNOWN;         // 0
/*  BC*/ uint32_t UNKNOWN;         // 0a 00 00 64

/*  C0*/ uint32_t UNKNOWN;         // 0a 00 00 64
         uint32_t UNKNOWN;         // c5 c0 00 80
         uint32_t UNKNOWN;         // 00 00 40 14

/*  CC*/ uint32_t mac1[2];

GAP

/* 103*/ char     prodName[85];    // "Broadcom NetXtreme Gigabit Ethernet Controller"
GAP
  tags...
  PN  Part Number
  EC
  SN  Serial Number
  MN  Model Number
  RV  Revision
  YA
  RW

/* 208*/ uint32_t mac2[2];

GAP

/* 258*/ uint32_t mac3[2];

44 bytes unknown
};

Note: the 0x0000_0007 field before the tags is considered part of the directory
by Broadcom, and the 0x2523_33D4 field is considered part of the "Bootstrap"
header:
  https://access.redhat.com/solutions/1302043
Looks like each of the regions (bootstrap, directory, manufacture, manufacture
II, boot code, second boot code) have their own CRC.

  ^_^ = officially confirmed using Broadcom header files
  ,,, = read by firmware

NOTE: looks like I got the tag format wrong, from the headers:
  uint32_t  sram_start_addr; // does not seem to be used or read though
  uint32_t  code_len; // and type
   // note: Remember how the length was 22 bits, not 24 bits?
   // Well:
   //   0x0008_0000  BMAPI_FW_CODE_IMAGE_EXECUTE_A
   //   0x0004_0000  BMAPI_FW_CODE_IMAGE_EXECUTE_B
  uint32_t  code_start_addr;

'Management Firmware' can be one of the following:
  ASF         (0x01)
  ASF_2_0     (0x02)
  IPMI        (0x04)
  UMP         (0x08)
  DASH        (0x10)
  NCSI        (0x20)

  VERSIONS:
    "5719-v1.39"      The 5720 image I used at first
    "5719-v1.43"      The Talos image below
    "5719-v1.45"      The image from the card I have

note: GEN 1E4 now thought to be BM_FW_FEATURE_CONFIG.
  0xC5C0_0080 = ASF enable, lom_design=1, vaux_cutoff_delay=0b11, link_idle=1
                link_aware=1, link_speed_power=1
  0xC5C0_0000 = same but no ASF enable
